Nockamixon Twp. v. Nockamixon Twp. Zoning Hearing Bd.


No. 1055 C.D. 2010


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


8 A.3d 434; 2010 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 616


October 14, 2010, Argued 
November 18, 2010, Decided 
November 18, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Nockamixon Twp. v. Nockamixon Twp. Zoning Hearing Bd., 2011 Pa. LEXIS 1714 (Pa., July 28, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. 09-02937-33-5. Common Pleas Court of the County of Bucks. Gibbons, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner challenged appellee township's zoning ordinances; a zoning hearing board (ZHB) sustained the challenge. The township appealed. The Bucks County Common Pleas Court (Pennsylvania) reversed the ZHB's decision; the owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owner contended the ordinances were void ab initio because they were improperly enacted by the township. The trial court found that although timely notice was not given for the meeting to adopt the 1968 ordinance, meetings and public notice about them were extensive, and the proposed ordinance was available for public inspection. While the 1990 ordinance was not recorded in as required by the law then in effect, it was maintained as a public record by the township and became part of its code book by virtue of a later codification. The trial court found the procedural defects did not violate due process, as the township provided sufficient notice of the proposed ordinances to insure an opportunity to be heard. It found that invalidating such longstanding ordinances would cause greater harm than was implicated by their enforcement. The appellate court agreed, and held that the later codification cured any defect in the prior recording of the 1990 ordinance. As owner participated in the meetings and there was no showing of prejudice, the defects did not implicate due process or other constitutional rights to the extent necessary to trigger the void ab initio doctrine.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was affirmed.

Ultimately, the court rejected the city's request to vacate the entire award and made various modification to bring it in compliance with the Recovery Plan.

City of Scranton v. Fire Fighters Local Union No. 60


No. 2342 C.D. 2009, No. 2442 C.D. 2009


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


8 A.3d 930; 2010 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 572


June 21, 2010, Argued 
October 29, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at City of Scranton v. Fire Fighters Local Union No. 60, 20 A.3d 525, 2011 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 157 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2011)
Vacated by, Remanded by City of Scranton v. Fire Fighters Local Union No. 60, 2012 Pa. LEXIS 320 (Pa., Feb. 15, 2012)
Appeal denied by City of Scranton v. Fire Fighters Local Union No. 60, 2012 Pa. LEXIS 317 (Pa., Feb. 15, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. 08 CV 8602. Common Pleas Court of the County of Lackawanna. O'Brien, Senior Judge.
City of Scranton v. E.B. Jermyn Lodge No. 2 of the FOP, 8 A.3d 971, 2010 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 574 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a city, its allied intervenors, and a firefighters union, sought review of an order of the Lackawanna County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania), which denied the city's petition to vacate an interest arbitration award. The trial court modified the wage, health insurance benefits, and pensions provisions of the award.


OVERVIEW: The city was a "financially distressed municipality" under the Municipalities Financial Recovery Act, 53 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 11701.101-11701.501, and a recovery plan was developed that included requirements for the city's employees. Thereafter, when the city and the firefighters reached an impasse in negotiations for a collective bargaining agreement (CBA), the matter was submitted to arbitration. An interest award was modified in order to comply with the plan. After another impasse for the next CBA, another interest arbitration award was made. The trial court modified the award in order to comply with the terms of the plan. Such modifications included wage, health insurance benefits, and pensions provisions. On appeal, the court made further modifications. It noted that prospective wage increases did not violate the plan. The health insurance increases in the award did not exceed the cap in the plan. Provisions of the staffing requirements that unduly interfered with the city's managerial prerogatives were voided, and cost containment measures were included. Modifications to the pension plan violated 53 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 30495(b) by allowing a pension in excess of the highest limit.


OUTCOME: The court modified the trial court order by reinstating the mid-year wages increases for the years 2009 through 2014, modifying the date for deletion of health care benefits for retirees, and voiding certain staffing requirements. It also included the mandatory cost containment provisions, and vacated the pension plan provisions. As modified, the court affirmed the trial court order.

 

1761 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Kovler v. Bureau of Admin. Adjudication


No. 579 C.D. 2010


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


6 A.3d 1060; 2010 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 557


July 16, 2010, Submitted 
October 19, 2010, Decided 
October 19, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Kovler v. Bureau of Admin. Adjudication, 2011 Pa. LEXIS 851 (Pa., Apr. 5, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. 01010, August Term 2009. Common Pleas Court of the County of Philadelphia. Fox, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver appealed an order entered by the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the decision of appellee Philadelphia Bureau of Administrative Adjudication (BAA), which found the driver liable for a parking citation and assessed fines and penalties totaling $ 61.00.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that the BAA's procedures were not unconstitutional because only the hearing examiner had the authority to compel the ticket writer's presence at the hearing under Philadelphia, Pa., Code § 12-2807(2). It was disingenuous for the driver to claim that he was denied the opportunity to cross-examine the ticket writer as he never requested the ticket writer's presence, and failed to raise any issue that would have required the ticket writer's presence. The driver did not challenge the date and time, location, or reason for the citation, or any other information provided by the ticket writer. The ticket writer's absence from the hearing did not violate due process. The driver did not have a right of confrontation. The absence of the original ticket from the record, assuming it was required under § 12-2807(2), was harmless error. The driver did not refute that he received the ticket, and presented photographs showing his vehicle parked in a stopping prohibited zone on the date and time in question. The driver admitted that his vehicle was partially parked in a stopping prohibited zone. The hearing examiner's decision was supported by substantial evidence.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

1762 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Pa. Builders Ass'n v. Dep't of Labor & Indus.


No. 27 M.D. 2010


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


4 A.3d 215; 2010 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 469


June 23, 2010, Argued 
August 25, 2010, Decided 
August 25, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Court of ORIGINAL JURISDICTION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Labor & Industry (L&I), filed preliminary objections to the amended petition for review filed by petitioners, a building association, several developers, and builders. Also before the court was the application for summary relief filed by petitioners. Petitioners sought a declaration that the 2009 Pennsylvania's Uniform Construction Code (UCC) and related codes were null and void.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners asserted in their petition for review that the 2009 UCC and other related codes were null and void as violative of Pa. Const. art. II, § 1 and sought to enjoin the L&I from enforcing the codes, plus other relief. Petitioners claimed that the new and amended provisions of the 2009 codes, especially the sprinkler requirements, had the effect of increasing the cost of an average newly-constructed home by approximately $ 15,000 and averred that the additional costs will have a significant impact on the demand for their home building and remodeling services. The court held that the post-UCC Review and Advisory Council Pennsylvania Construction Code Act (PCCA), 35 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 7210.101-7210.1103, neither improperly delegated the Pennsylvania General Assembly's rule-making authority, nor its authority over the execution and administration of that law. So, the L&I's adoption of the International Code Council's 2009 codes as Pennsylvania's 2009 UCC did not violate Pa. Const. art. II, § 1. Thus, petitioners failed to overcome their burden of demonstrating that the PCCA clearly, palpably, and plainly violated the Pennsylvania Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the L&I's preliminary objections. The court further determined that by sustaining the L&I's preliminary objections, petitioners' amended petition for review was dismissed and was no longer before the court. Therefore, petitioners' application for summary relief was dismissed as moot.

Golovach v. DOT, Bureau of Driver Licensing


No. 2532 C.D. 2009


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


4 A.3d 759; 2010 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 458


May 14, 2010, Submitted 
August 19, 2010, Decided 
August 19, 2010, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. SA 1106-09. Common Pleas Court of the County of Allegheny. Gallo, Senior Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of Transportation, Bureau of Driver Licensing, sought review of the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which sustained the appeal of appellee licensee from the Department's decision recalling his driver's license pursuant to 67 Pa. Code § 83.5(a)(2)(i).


OVERVIEW: The Department received a cardiologist's "Initial Reporting Form," DL 13, indicating that licensee suffered from intermittent complete heart block and that the condition affected his ability to safely operate a motor vehicle. The Department notified licensee that it was recalling his driver's license indefinitely. The Department enclosed a "Cardiovascular Form," DL-120, with the recall notice, which was completed by licensee's treating physician, who indicated that licensee had a heart block for which a pacemaker had been implanted, and that licensee was physically competent to operate a motor vehicle. The appellate court held that, contrary to the Department's contentions, the trial court correctly held that prior case law established that 67 Pa. Code § 83.49(a) created an impermissible irrebuttable presumption. In addition, the doctor's reports constituted substantial evidence in support of the trial court's decision.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.


 

1764 of 2746 DOCUMENTS



Osborne Assocs. v. Unemployment Comp. Bd. of Review


No. 2084 C.D. 2009


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


3 A.3d 722; 2010 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 450; Unemployment Ins. Rep. (CCH) P12,567


May 17, 2010, Argued 
August 13, 2010, Decided 
August 13, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Osborne Assocs. v. Unemployment Comp. Bd. of Review, 2012 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 13 (Pa. Commw. Ct., Jan. 10, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. B-489180. State Agency: Unemployment Compensation Board of Review.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employer sought review of an order from respondent, the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review (Pennsylvania), which affirmed an unemployment compensation referee's decision. The referee had determined that a claimant was not disqualified from receiving unemployment compensation benefits (UCBs) under § 402(h) of the Unemployment Compensation Law (UCL), 43 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 802(h).


OVERVIEW: The claimant was a cosmetologist for a hair salon. She applied for UCBs after her hours were reduced. While working part-time, she also provided services for the employer. The claimant reported earnings from both workplaces. It was initially determined that the claimant was not disqualified from receiving UCBs. On review, the referee agreed, finding that an employer/employee relationship existed between the claimant and the employer. The Board also agreed, finding that the claimant was not an independent contractor (IC) for the employer. The Board did not apply the IC factors in holding that there was no disqualification under §§ 402(h) and 4(l)(2)(B) of the UCL, 43 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 802(h) and 753(l)(2)(B). On further review, the court held that the Board erred in interpreting the Cosmetology Law, 63 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 507-527, and regulations to determine whether the claimant was an employee or an IC instead of applying the factors typically considered under the IC test. The Board could consider 63 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 514 as well as 49 Pa. Code §§ 7.81, 7.82, and 7.83 in assessing whether the employer had the right to review the claimant's work or monitor her performance.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order of the Board, and remanded the matter for a new adjudication by the Board that addressed the IC test.


 

1765 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Court of Common Pleas of Lackawanna County v. Pa. Office of Open Records


No. 35 M.D. 2010


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


2 A.3d 810; 2010 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 448


July 9, 2010, Submitted 
August 11, 2010, Decided 
August 11, 2010, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Court of Common Pleas, through the Administrative Office of Pennsylvania Courts (AOPC), sought a declaratory judgment that respondent Office of Open Records (OOR) did not have the jurisdiction to force the County to provide e-mails and correspondence from the Director of the County Office of Domestic Relations to certain requestors pursuant to the Right-to-Know Law (RTKL), 65 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 67.101-67.3104. AOPC sought an injunction.


OVERVIEW: The requestors sought inappropriate e-mails from or to any e-mail accounts used by a County employee, who was also a court employee, related to his suspension. The County denied the request. The OOR granted the requestors' appeal and ordered the County to release the records. The court held the fact that the employee was paid by the County did not affect his status as a judicial employee. Likewise, the fact that the County had access to the employee's e-mails because it provided the County's court computer system was irrelevant. Just because the County provided logistic support to the courts did not mean that every record stored on what the County provided as part of its function to support the court made it a County record. Otherwise, every record ever generated by a County court, including the draft opinions and law clerk memorandums, would be accessible through the RTKL simply by submitting the request to the County instead, an absurd result that would make 65 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 67.304. of the RTKL meaningless. Besides violating the RTKL, AOPC was correct that the OOR's order constituted a blatant and unconstitutional violation of the separation of powers doctrine.


OUTCOME: AOPC's motion for summary relief was granted, and the OOR and County were permanently enjoined from releasing any information, documents or materials that in any way pertain to the employee or other judicial employees that were responsive to the requestors' requests.

Callowhill Ctr. Assocs., LLC v. Zoning Bd. of Adjustment

Whymeyer v. Dep't of State, Bureau of Prof'l & Occupational Affairs


No. 1525 C.D. 2008


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


997 A.2d 1254; 2010 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 304


March 31, 2009, Argued 
June 22, 2010, Decided 
June 22, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. 1435-47-2007. State Agency: Department of State.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relying on 63 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 151.2(b)(1)(i) of the Pennsylvania Engineer, Land, Surveyor and Geologist Registration Law and 49 Pa. Code § 37.1, respondent, the Pennsylvania Registration Board for Professional Engineers, Land Surveyors and Geologists, denied petitioner applicant's appeal of the provisional denial of his application to sit for the fundamentals of engineering examination. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: After a university awarded petitioner a Bachelor of Science degree in electrical engineering, he applied to sit for the engineering exam. The Board voted provisionally to deny his application because the Accreditation Board in Engineering and Technology (ABET) had not accredited the university's electrical engineering program. He appealed; at the hearing, a university professor opined that due to an increase in the number of faculty members currently devoted to the program, it would satisfy the ABET criteria, but the university had not re-applied for ABET accreditation due to the cost involved. The Board deferred to ABET and denied the appeal. The court held that while a person of ordinary intelligence could reasonably believe that a four-year degree from an accredited university satisfied the Board's standard set forth in 49 Pa. Code § 37.1, the regulation was not void on its face. But because the Board did not exercise its independent statutory authority to evaluate the university's electrical engineering program, but specifically declined to do so, relying exclusively on the lack of ABET accreditation, 49 Pa. Code § 37.1 was unconstitutionally applied.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the Board and remanded the matter to the Board with directions to permit petitioner, upon application, to sit for the fundamentals of engineering examination.

Messina v. E. Penn Twp.


No. 1919 C.D. 2009


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


995 A.2d 517; 2010 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 257


March 17, 2010, Argued 
May 26, 2010, Decided 
May 26, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Messina v. E. Penn Twp., 607 Pa. 623, 9 A.3d 1136, 2010 Pa. LEXIS 2836 (2010)
Affirmed by Messina v. E. Penn Twp., 2012 Pa. LEXIS 2905 (Pa., Dec. 17, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. 2254 CV 2008. Common Pleas Court of the County of Carbon. Black, Senior Judge.
Messina v. E. Penn Twp., 2009 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 90 (2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challengers sought review of the order of the Common Pleas Court of the County of Carbon (Pennsylvania), which upheld a zoning ordinance enacted 12 years earlier. The challengers filed its procedural validity challenge against appellee township, pursuant to the Pennsylvania Municipalities Planning Code, 53 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 11002-A(b), and the Judicial Code, 42 Pa.C.S. § 5571.1(a). Intervenor objectors were also parties.


OVERVIEW: The challengers owned land in the township, which they used as a quarry. The zoning ordinance at issue was enacted in 1996 and established a comprehensive zoning scheme that restricted the use and development of the land in the township. In upholding the validity of the zoning ordinance at issue, the trial court rejected the challengers' attempt to hold the ordinance void ab initio. The court emphasized that the challengers declined the offer of a hearing on their procedural validity challenge. As a result, the challengers did not prove the existence of a procedural defect affecting notice or due process concerns. The court held that the challengers did not rebut a statutory presumption that the township and its landowners substantially relied on the validity and effectiveness of the zoning ordinance over the 12 years between enactment of the zoning ordinance and the procedural validity challenge. Therefore, the court declined to declare the ordinance void ab initio. Since the challengers refused to have a hearing, the court was unable to determine if the change to the ordinance on the night it was enacted was substantial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

Grimaud v. Pa. Ins. Dep't


No. 1683 C.D. 2009


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


995 A.2d 391; 2010 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 216


February 5, 2010, Submitted 
April 28, 2010, Decided 
April 28, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. CL07-04-036. State Agency: Insurance Department.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner logging company, a sole proprietorship, sought review of an adjudication and order of respondent Insurance Commissioner of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania who affirmed a determination by respondent Appeals Subcommittee of the Pennsylvania Compensation Rating Bureau (PCRB) which denied the company's challenge to its business's classification for purposes of calculating its workers' compensation insurance premium.


OVERVIEW: The company purchased and harvested timber, and hauled and marketed logs. It had its own log truck, which it principally used to haul its logs from its staging areas to saw mills and pulp mills. Historically, either the owner or a logging employee drove the log truck. The company had only one employee, a part-time truck driver, who did not perform any other logging or logging-related activities. The company asked that its classification be changed to Code 811. The PCRB took the position that the company had been properly classified in Code 009. The Commissioner rejected the company's appeal and found that any hardship or perceived unfairness was self-inflicted to some extent as the company switched its workers' compensation carrier and hired an employee rather than outsource the job to an independent hauler. The court found that the record supported the Commissioner's reasoning. While advocating for its preferred classification system over the PCRB classification system, the company failed to explain how the PCRB system actually violated the Workers' Compensation Act or the Insurance Company Law of 1921 and was thus ultra vires. Nor did it show any constitutional violation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Commissioner was affirmed.

Nieves v. Pa. Bd. of Prob. & Parole


No. 113 M.D. 2009


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


995 A.2d 412; 2010 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 214


January 29, 2010, Submitted 
April 28, 2010, Decided 
April 28, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed without opinion by Nieves v. Pa. Bd. of Prob. & Parole, 2011 Pa. LEXIS 3082 (Pa., Dec. 21, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Court of ORIGINAL JURISDICTION.
Nieves v. Pa. Bd. of Prob. & Parole, 983 A.2d 236, 2009 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1532 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner filed a petition for review in the court's original jurisdiction against the Pennsylvania Board of Probation and Parole. The prisoner and the Board each sought summary relief. The prisoner sought an order in mandamus compelling the Board to issue an order releasing him on parole.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was a convicted sex offender. The Board issued a decision to parole the prisoner to a Community Corrections Center upon his completion of a sex offender program. The prisoner was placed on a waiting list. Following the adoption of new procedures, the Board modified its decision and stated that the prisoner would be released on parole upon completion of a sex offender program. The Board rejected all of the prisoner's home plan proposals because the residences were too close to schools. The Board argued that 61 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 315 was inconsistent with the Parole Act and § 35 of the Parole Act repealed all parts of acts that were inconsistent with the Parole Act. The court agreed with the Board. To the extent the prisoner would construe 61 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 315 to require the Board to release him on parole simply because he served his minimum sentence, 61 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 315 was inconsistent with the Parole Act. Because the Board had no duty to issue a release order for the prisoner pursuant to 61 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 315, the Board was entitled to summary relief. The Board's modification of its decision did not violate the ex post facto rights of the prisoner.


OUTCOME: The application by the Board for summary relief was granted. The prisoner's application was denied.

Pa. Med. Soc'y v. Dep't of Pub. Welfare


No. 584 M.D. 2008, No. 585 M.D. 2008


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


994 A.2d 33; 2010 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 194


February 10, 2010, Argued 
April 15, 2010, Decided 
April 15, 2010, Filed

Court of ORIGINAL JURISDICTION.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner health care providers sought summary relief in an action against respondents, the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania and various Commonwealth entities, alleging that funds were not properly provided and transferred to the Fund established under the Medical Care Availability and Reduction of Error (MCARE) Act, 40 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 1303.101-1303.1115, in violation of the Uniformity Clause of the Pennsylvania Constitution.


OVERVIEW: The providers filed their suit, alleging that although abatements continued to be granted under the Health Care Provider Retention (HCPR) Program (Abatement Law), 40 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 1303.1101-1303.1115 (after repeal of prior law and reenactment), and revenues to fund the awarded abatements continued to accumulate in the HCPR, none of those funds were transferred to the MCARE Fund after a period of time. Although preliminary objections filed by the Commonwealth had been previously overruled for the most part, the question presented on the merits was not ruled upon. Ann. § 201(1) did not provide a limitation on the Department of Public Welfare's authority to transfer funds. The providers had standing and vested rights to the abatements.


OUTCOME: The court granted the providers' application for summary relief.

Int'l Ass'n v. City of Chester


No. 1404 C.D. 2009


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


991 A.2d 1001; 2010 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 138; 188 L.R.R.M. 2501; 159 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P60,965


February 8, 2010, Argued 
March 22, 2010, Decided 
March 22, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Int'l Ass'n of Firefighters Local 1400 v. City of Chester, 2011 Pa. LEXIS 157 (Pa., Jan. 20, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. 08-14468. Common Pleas Court of the County of Delaware. Proud, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant union challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania), which granted appellee city's petition to set aside an Act 111, 43 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 217.1-217.10, grievance arbitration award. The union had filed a grievance alleging the city violated a parity provision in a 2002-06 collective bargaining agreement (CBA) by failing to pay them the 3 percent wage increase given to the police in 2007, plus $ 500.


OVERVIEW: The union consisted of firefighters. Of significance, the city was a distressed municipality subject to the Municipalities Financial Recovery Act (Act 47), 53 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 11701.101-11701.501, and an implemented 2006 Recovery Plan. The arbitration award sustained the union's grievance and directed the city to pay the union members the three percent wage increase plus an additional $ 500 wage increase. In attempting to set aside the arbitration award, the city argued that the arbitrator exceeded his power since the CBA expired at the end of 2006 and the economic provisions in expired contracts did not carry over in the absence of a new agreement. The trial court agreed, finding that economic terms, including wage increase provisions, of expired contracts did not carry over in the absence of a new agreement. The court held that Act 47 and the 2006 Recovery Plan could be applied to a wage increase awarded for a year after the term of an expired CBA. However, to the extent the arbitrator directed the city to violate the 2006 Recovery Plan and thereby also violate Act 47, he required the city to perform an illegal act, which was in excess of his powers.


OUTCOME: The court modified the order of the trial court by holding that the city could voluntarily grant a 3 percent wage increase, but it could not voluntarily grant a wage increase greater than 3 percent, thus, the award granting an additional wage increase of $ 500 was set aside, and only wage increases in conformance with the 2006 Recovery Plan were permitted. As modified, the court otherwise affirmed.

BPG Real Estate Investors-Straw Party II, L.P. v. Bd. of Supervisors


No. 777 C.D. 2009


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


990 A.2d 140; 2010 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 111


February 8, 2010, Argued 
March 5, 2010, Decided 
March 5, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by BPG Real Estate Investors-Straw Party II, L.P. v. Bd. of Supervisors, 611 Pa. 628, 23 A.3d 543, 2011 Pa. LEXIS 1368 (2011)
Appeal denied by BPG Real Estate Investors-Straw Party II, L.P. v. Bd. of Supervisors, 611 Pa. 628, 23 A.3d 543, 2011 Pa. LEXIS 1369 (2011)
Related proceeding at Newtown Square East, L.P. v. Nat'l Realty Corp., 38 A.3d 1018, 2011 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 617 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2011)
Related proceeding at Newtown Square East, L.P. v. Twp. of Newtown, 38 A.3d 1008, 2011 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 618 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2011)
Related proceeding at de Botton v. Kaplin, 2012 Phila. Ct. Com. Pl. LEXIS 189 (2012)
Related proceeding at Newton Square East, L.P. v. Twp. of Newtown, 2014 Pa. LEXIS 3080 (Pa., Nov. 24, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. 07-12998 and 07-12999. Common Pleas Court of the County of Delaware. Proud, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A neighboring landowner appealed the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania) erred in approving a settlement agreement between the developers and the Board of Supervisors. The neighboring landowner argued the settlement agreement constituted unlawful contract zoning and/or spot zoning. In addition, the neighboring landowner asserted the settlement agreement infringed on its procedural due process rights.


OVERVIEW: The settlement agreement allowed for development of a developer's 51-acre property which was the subject of a land use appeal and a mandamus action. The settlement agreement also permitted mixed-use development on adjoining properties owned by the other developers. The total acreage affected by the settlement agreement was 219 acres. The appellate court concluded the trial court lacked authority to approve development of that portion of the subject properties beyond the 51-acre tract at issue in the underlying litigation. Therefore, the trial court's authority was limited to review of the supervisors' handling of the conditional use application, which was brought up on appeal. By approving the settlement agreement, which allowed for development of other properties owned by other entities who were not involved in the appealed conditional use decision, the trial court exceeded its statutory scope of review. The spot zoning claim was rejected as it related to the 51-acre portion of the properties. The settlement agreement did not result in a violation of its procedural due process rights as it related to the 51-acre portion of the subject properties.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was reversed to the extent it approved development of that portion of the subject properties beyond the 51-acre tract at issue in the underlying litigation. The matter was remanded to the trial court for consideration of whether to approve that portion of the settlement agreement that related only to development of the 51-acre tract at issue or to reject the settlement agreement in its entirety.

United States Orgs. for Bankr. Alternatives, Inc. v. Dep't of Banking


No. 69 M.D. 2009


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


991 A.2d 370; 2010 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 80


November 25, 2009, Submitted 
February 25, 2010, Decided 
February 25, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by United States Orgs. for Bankr. Alternatives, Inc. v. Dep't of Banking, 2011 Pa. LEXIS 1894 (Pa., Aug. 15, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: United States Orgs. for Bankr. Alternatives, Inc. v. Dep't of Banking, 2009 Pa. Commw. Unpub. LEXIS 496 (2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a debt service provider, filed a summary relief application against respondents, the Department of Banking (DOB) (Pennsylvania) and the Secretary thereof, seeking a judgment declaring that all sections of the Debt Management Services Act, 63 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 2401-2449, were unconstitutional as applied to debt settlement service providers.


OVERVIEW: The Act granted the DOB broad powers to regulate debt settlement and debt management service providers. It was noted that respondents' prior request to dismiss the petition for failure to state a claim had been denied. At that time, the court stated that the Act granted a standardless delegation of authority to the DOB with respect to the regulation and setting of fees for providers. Although the DOB had not yet promulgated regulations, the matter was ripe for judicial review because the provider made a facial challenge to the Act itself. Respondents failed to support their claim that factual issues were in dispute that prevented adjudication. Moreover, the question of statutory interpretation was one of law. The court found that previously, it was determined that the Act set forth sufficient standards to support the authority of the DOB to require licensure of providers. However, 63 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 2403(b) was unconstitutional, as the DOB lacked authority to promulgate regulations affecting providers. Similarly, the lack of standards in 63 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 2415(h) rendered it unconstitutional. However, there were adequate policy choices as to licensing of providers.


OUTCOME: The court granted the provider's application in part, declaring two specific sections of the Act unconstitutional and unenforceable. The remainder of the application was denied.

 

1776 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. 542 Ont. St., Bethlehem, PA.


No. 1657 C.D. 2008


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


989 A.2d 411; 2010 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 74


November 5, 2009, Argued 
February 17, 2010, Decided 
February 17, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Commonwealth v. 542 Ont. St., 2011 Pa. LEXIS 175 (Pa., Jan. 25, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. Misc. No. 4549-2005. Common Pleas Court of the County of Northampton. Giordano, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Commonwealth filed a petition for forfeiture against appellant real property owner, who had been acquitted of drug-related criminal charges. The Common Pleas Court of the County of Northampton (Pennsylvania) granted the Commonwealth's petition. Appellant challenged the trial court's decision.


OVERVIEW: Appellant first argued that the Controlled Substances Forfeiture Act, 42 Pa.C.S. §§ 6801-6802, directed that the Rules of Civil Procedure applied in forfeiture proceedings and that the Commonwealth was required to comply with the service provisions in the rules. The court stated that the provisions in 42 Pa.C.S. § 6802 provided a framework that ensured sufficient notice to an owner. Next, it was not necessary that a forfeiture be supported by an underlying criminal conviction. With regard to whether the forfeiture of appellant's house violated the Excessive Fines Clause of U.S. Const. amend. VIII, the value of appellant's house, $65,000, was not grossly disproportionate to the maximum penalty for the conspiracy, $100,000. Furthermore, there was no error in the trial court's conclusion that appellant's violation was part of a pattern of misbehavior. As for the harm resulting from appellant's conduct, the record supported the trial court's findings that the harm caused to society by drug trafficking was self-evident, that appellant's property exacted a heavy toll from government resources; and the harm resulting from appellant's property was widespread.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Plaxton v. Lycoming County Zoning Hearing Bd.

CASE SUMMARY:

Getz v. Pa. Bd. of Prob. & Parole


No. 1060 C.D. 2009


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


984 A.2d 1036; 2009 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1588


October 30, 2009, Submitted 
November 19, 2009, Decided 
November 19, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. Parole No. 134-CC. State Agency: Board of Probation and Parole.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of an order from respondent, the Pennsylvania Board of Probation and Parole, which denied his request for administrative relief and recommitted him for violations of his parole. The inmate had been previously convicted of aggravated indecent assault.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was sentenced to imprisonment for his sex offense conviction. He was released on supervised parole with the mandate that he have no contact with minor females, and that he not possess certain child photographs, and not have videos without permission. During a search by parole agents of the inmate's apartment, children's DVDs, a knife, and a camera containing photographs of a child were found. At a parole violation hearing, the inmate provided explanations for each item found. The Board recommitted the inmate to imprisonment as a technical parole violator. The inmate's request for administrative relief was denied. On appeal, the court found that unlike 18 Pa.C.S. § 6312(d), the special condition regarding the photographs was violated where the camera held digital images of a child, whether the image was processed into a photograph or not. The inmate's explanation that his knife was a "displayed curio" was not deemed credible. Rather, he possessed a weapon which was a violation of his parole. The Board failed to show that the DVDs were obviously and notoriously directed at children where there was no evidence as to each DVD's content, rating, and marketing audience.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the Board.

Ballroom, LLC v. Commonwealth


No. 1948 C.D. 2008


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


984 A.2d 582; 2009 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1579


February 13, 2009, Submitted 
November 17, 2009, Decided 
November 17, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. 14349-2008. Common Pleas Court of the County of Erie. Connelly, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff ballroom challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County (Pennsylvania), which sustained the preliminary objections of defendant, the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, and dismissed its action against it and defendants, a county district attorney, a health department, and a township police department. The complaint sought to enjoin the enforcement of the Clean Indoor Air Act, 35 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 637.1 - 637.11.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff operated a bingo hall and sought an injunction to prohibit defendants from enforcing the Act. Plaintiff primarily contended that the Act was unconstitutional. The trial court sustained the preliminary objections of defendants for lack of jurisdiction upon concluding that the court had original and exclusive jurisdiction over the matter since the case involved the Commonwealth as a party. The court noted some procedural errors committed by the trial court and held that the Commonwealth was not an indispensable party in the action and that it did not have original jurisdiction over the action as pled. The court noted that simply naming the Commonwealth as a party, without naming any state agency, was insufficient to state a claim against a Commonwealth agency, specifically those agencies charged by the Commonwealth to enforce the Act. However, the court found that plaintiff sufficiently averred that the local agencies named as defendants were charged with enforcement of the Act and that the requested injunctive relief, if found to be warranted, could be awarded without participation in the action by any state entity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the action against the Commonwealth, but reversed its dismissal of the action as to the remaining defendants and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings against the named local agencies.

Crews v. City of Chester


No. 1182 C.D. 2008


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


983 A.2d 829; 2009 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1554


June 11, 2009, Argued 
November 2, 2009, Decided 
November 2, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Summary judgment granted by, in part, Motion denied by Crews v. City of Chester, 2012 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 36 (Pa. Commw. Ct., Jan. 25, 2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a mother on behalf of her minor son and individually, sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania), which determined that the minor lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of Chester, Pa., Ordinance art. 711, which was an anti-loitering ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The minor walked to a variety store that was in a "high drug activity area." After he purchased snacks, he remained in the area, talking with other individuals. When two police officers on bikes approached, the minor and the others ran away. However, the minor stopped running and when one of the officers caught up to him, he allegedly cursed at the minor, struck him, and knocked him down. The minor was arrested and charged with loitering, in violation of art. 711. The criminal matter was dismissed for failure to prosecute, and the minor and his mother filed their civil action. The trial court upheld the constitutionality of art. 711 and dismissed the officer with prejudice. After an initial appeal was filed, the trial court vacated the prior order and dismissed the remaining claims. On appeal therefrom, the court held that the trial court erred in finding that the minor lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of art. 711. The minor suffered an injury directly attributable to art. 711, despite the fact that the charge was dismissed. Accordingly, he had standing to raise the issue. As the trial court did not consider the constitutionality issue, a remand was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

Hawk v. Eldred Twp. Bd. of Supervisors

September 17, 2009, Argued

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reargument denied by Hawk v. Eldred Twp. Bd. of Supervisors, 2009 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1590 (Pa. Commw. Ct., Nov. 20, 2009)
Appeal denied by Hawk v. Eldred Twp. Bd. of Supervisors, 2010 Pa. LEXIS 2790 (Pa., Dec. 1, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. 9915 CV 2008. Common Pleas Court of the County of Monroe. Zulick, J.
Hawk v. Eldred Twp. Zoning Hearing Bd., 978 A.2d 1085, 2009 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 785 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Monroe County (Pennsylvania), which denied his land use appeal seeking to have a zoning ordinance declared void ab initio for failure by appellee township to follow proper statutory procedures when adopting it and he sought to have 42 Pa.C.S. § 5571.1 declared unconstitutional because it restricted him from contesting the adoption of the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The landowner had a 21.27 acre parcel of property in a commercial zoning district and began operating a race track on the land, which was not a permitted use in a commercial zoning district. A zoning enforcement notice citing the landowner for the race track operation without a zoning permit was issued. The township denied the landowner's appeal for a permit, which was affirmed by the trial court. The landowner filed another appeal challenging the method by which the ordinance was enacted. The court held that because the landowner did not raise a procedural challenge regarding the ordinance in his first appeal, the issue was waived. The court held that even if the landowner had not waived the procedural attack on the ordinance and had been able to properly raise it in his second appeal, he still would not prevail on any of his alternative theories. Specifically, the trial court properly applied 42 Pa.C.S. § 5571.1 and the landowner had every opportunity for years to attend a meeting and for months to view the ordinance and could have challenged it from its inception but he did not. By waiting four years, he was found time barred from challenging the validity of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court denying the landowner's appeal.

Pa. Bankers Ass'n v. Pa. Dep't of Banking


No. 42 M.D. 2005, No. 98 M.D. 2005, No. 157 C.D. 2005


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


981 A.2d 975; 2009 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1485


June 10, 2009, Argued 
September 28, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No.: Original Jurisdiction and App-2003-01, App-2003-02. State Agency: Department of Banking.
Pa. Bankers Ass'n v. Pa. Dep't of Banking, 598 Pa. 313, 956 A.2d 956, 2008 Pa. LEXIS 1544 (2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania remanded the instant matter upon reversing a decision, finding that petitioners, banks and a bankers' association, lacked standing as intervenors in a proceeding, wherein respondent, the Pennsylvania Department of Banking (PDB), determined that respondents, two state-chartered credit unions (CUs), could convert their fields of membership pursuant to the Credit Union Code, 17 Pa.C.S. §§ 101-1504.


OVERVIEW: Each of the CUs had a field of membership that consisted of select employer groups, and each sought charter conversion to serve a community field of membership based on, inter alia, the five-county geographical zone. A presiding officer for the PDB did not allow disclosure of all the CUs' documents to petitioners. It was determined that the five-county area constituted a "well-defined local community" under 12 U.S.C.S. § 1759(g)(1) and 17 Pa.C.S. § 501(e)(2) for each CU, and that petitioners' interests were not adversely impacted by the conversions. On appeal, the Supreme Court reversed that decision, finding that petitioners had standing as a public interest party. On remand, the court found no evidentiary ruling error by the PDB. Substantial evidence supported the PDB's finding under § 1759(g)(1) and § 501(e)(2) regarding a well-defined local community. The PDB properly handled the issue of tax consequences, made sufficient findings, and the improper taking of official notice was only harmless error. There was no due process violation by the failure to disclose all documents and information under 71 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 733-302(A)(2).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the PDB.

Northeastern Pa. Imaging Ctr. v. Commonwealth


No. 635 F.R. 2007


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


978 A.2d 1055; 2009 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 772


March 30, 2009, Argued 
July 29, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by Northeastern Pa. Imaging Ctr. v. Commonwealth, 2011 Pa. LEXIS 3087 (Pa., Dec. 21, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. 0624876. State Agency: Board of Finance and Revenue.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner business sought review of an adjudication of respondent, the Pennsylvania Board of Finance and Revenue, which denied its petition for a refund of Pennsylvania sales tax it paid for the acquisition and installation of a magnetic resonance imaging (MRI) system and a positron emission tomography/computerized tomography (PET/CT Scan) system.


OVERVIEW: The business asserted that the equipment was installed in connection with a construction contract and thereafter became a part of the real estate. Given those circumstances, the business asserted that it was the obligation of its vendor to pay a use tax on the wholesale price of the equipment, and it was not the business's obligation to pay a sales tax on the retail price of the equipment, as found by the Board. The court found merit in the business's position and reversed the Board upon finding that the MRI and PET/CT Scan systems were real estate structures within the meaning of the Tax Reform Code of 1971, 72 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 7201(nn). The court found that the business met its burden of showing an intention that the systems became a permanent part of the real estate as each system satisfied the three factors established in case law for a chattel that could be either personalty or realty. The court found that the business's evidence supported the conclusion that the chattels in the case, namely the MRI and PET/CT Scan systems, constituted realty, not personalty.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the adjudication of the Board denying the business's petition for a refund of the sales tax.

1700 Columbus Assocs. v. City of Philadelphia, Zoning Bd. of Adjustment

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant City appealed an order entered by the Common Pleas Court of the County of Philadelphia (Pennsylvania), which reversed the denial by the Zoning Board of Adjustment of the City of Philadelphia (ZBA) of appellee applicant's request for a variance, and granted the variance.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that the applicant did not show that the uses already permitted rendered the property valueless or incapable of being leased. The erroneous findings that a mattress showroom and an adult cabaret were on the property were not necessary to the lack of hardship finding, which was supported by the evidence. The applicant failed to preserve its constitutional claim based on free commercial speech. The distinction between onsite and offsite advertising billboards was permissible.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed, and the order of the ZBA was reinstated.

Stat. Ann. §§ 2401 - 2449, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners were two individual debt settlement services providers (DSS Providers) and a trade group representing a number of DSS Providers and asserted that Act 117 was unconstitutional on its face and as applied to DSS Providers for a number of reasons. Otherwise, the court overruled the remainder of the Department's preliminary objections since the challengers articulated their claims regarding Act 117 in a manner that it was possible they could be successful. Therefore, the action had to proceed on the merits of the challengers' claims.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the Department's first preliminary objection as to the challengers' civil rights violation claims and, otherwise, overruled the remainder of the Department's preliminary objections.

Cash Am. Net of Nev., LLC v. Dep't of Banking


No. 8 M.D. 2009


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


978 A.2d 1028; 2009 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 570


April 1, 2009, Argued 
July 10, 2009, Decided 
July 10, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Cash Am. Net of Nev., LLC v. Commonwealth, 2010 Pa. LEXIS 2386 (Pa., Oct. 19, 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner lender brought suit against respondents banking department (department) and secretary, seeking to have a notice issued by the secretary declared unlawful and to enjoin the department and the secretary from implementing or enforcing it. The department counterclaimed, seeking a declaration that the lender's internet lending to Pennsylvania residents was unlawful. All parties moved for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The notice advised that engaging in nonmortgage consumer lending to Pennsylvania residents by any means, including by means of the internet or by mail, was engaging in such business in Pennsylvania as contemplated by 7 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 6203. The lender argued initially that the notice was unlawful unpromulgated rulemaking. The court found that the notice merely interpreted § 6203 and revised the department's interpretation in prior letters. The manner of adopting the change was consistent with the department's enforcement authority, and it reserved some discretion. The notice thus properly represented a policy statement. Further, the department's current interpretation was correct. The language of § 6203 expanded coverage to encompass employees, agents, and brokers. The structure of § 6203 made it unlawful for any unlicensed person to engage in negotiating or making specified types of loans, and it defined the persons whose conduct may fit this activity. By making payday loans, the lender was violating the Consumer Discount Company Act (CDCA) and the Loan Interest and Protection Law (LIPL), 41 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 201, by lending to Pennsylvania residents without a license.


OUTCOME: The lender's application for summary relief was denied. The application for summary relief filed by the department and the secretary was granted. The court declared that the lender's operations were in violation of the CDCA and the LIPL. The court also declared that the lender's practice of making payday loans to Pennsylvania residents was not authorized by the laws of Pennsylvania and specifically violated the CDCA and LIPL.

D.E.L.T.A. Rescue v. Bureau of Charitable Orgs.

COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


979 A.2d 415; 2009 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 567

Appealed from No. 0017-98-06.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a California charitable organization, appealed the final order of the Secretary of the Commonwealth, which imposed an administrative fine of $ 3,000 against it and ordered it to cease its fundraising and solicitation within the Commonwealth. Respondent, the Pennsylvania Bureau of Charitable Organizations, asserted petitioner violated the Solicitation of Funds for Charitable Purposes Act, 10 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 162.1-.23.


OVERVIEW: The order required that petitioner to cease its fundraising and solicitation within the Commonwealth until it paid the fine and complied with the registration, notification, and disclosure requirements of the Act. Petitioner challenged the constitutionality of the Act in several regards, asserted that the Secretary's findings were not supported by substantial evidence, and claimed that the Bureau was estopped from enforcing the Act against it. 1789 of 2746 DOCUMENTS



Donnelly v. York County Bd. of Assessment Appeals


No. 1015 C.D. 2008


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


976 A.2d 1226; 2009 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 562


May 22, 2009, Submitted 
July 2, 2009, Decided 
July 2, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. 2007-SU-1554-Y08. Common Pleas Court of the County of York. DORNEY, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee county board of assessment appeals upheld the imposition and amount of the roll-back taxes imposed on appellant landowners, who appealed. The York County Common Pleas Court (Pennsylvania) held that the roll-back taxes were properly imposed under the Pennsylvania Farmland and Forest Land Assessment Act of 1974, 72 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 5490.1 - 5490.13. The landowners sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The tract at issue had enjoyed a "clean and green" preferential assessment under the Act for many years. After two of the landowners split off two acres from their parcel and deeded them to the third (their daughter), the county imposed roll-back taxes on all three landowners. The appellate court rejected the landowners' claim that the Act's provisions relating to roll-back taxes were unconstitutionally vague. Their theory that no roll-back taxes were owed by any of them ignored language in 72 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 5490.6(a.1)(2) that each tract that had been split off would be subject to rollback taxes and that the landowner changing the use of the land would be liable. This targeted the third landowner's tract, and placed the tax burden on her, assuming she was the one responsible for the change in the property's use. The Act imposed roll-back taxes where a split-off parcel had been conveyed to a third party, even though, as here, the use of the split-off parcel satisfied the criteria in § 5490.6(a.1)(1)(i).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

NRA v. City of Philadelphia


No. 1305 C.D. 2008, No. 1306 C.D. 2008


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


977 A.2d 78; 2009 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 470


November 12, 2008, Argued 
June 18, 2009, Decided 
June 18, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by NRA v. City of Phila., 2010 Pa. LEXIS 1237 (Pa., June 7, 2010)
Appeal denied by NRA v. City of Phila., 2010 Pa. LEXIS 1236 (Pa., June 7, 2010)
Appeal denied by NRA v. City of Philadelphia, 2010 Pa. LEXIS 1232 (Pa., June 7, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. 1472 April Term, 2008. Common Pleas Court of the County of Philadelphia. Greenspan, J.
NRA v. City of Phila., 2008 Phila. Ct. Com. Pl. LEXIS 159 (2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action brought by appellees, an association and its members, the Common Pleas Court of the County of Philadelphia (Pennsylvania) permanently enjoined appellant city from enforcing two ordinances regulating the transfer and possession of firearms. The trial court also found that the association and members lacked standing to challenge three additional gun control ordinances. The city appealed and the association and members cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The association and the members argued that the ordinances were unconstitutional and were preempted by 18 Pa.C.S. § 6120(a). The trial court permanently enjoined the city from enforcing ordinances which prohibited the possession, sale, and transfer of certain types of guns, including assault weapons, and which prohibited purchase of a handgun through a straw purchaser. Initially, the appellate court agreed with the trial court's ruling that the association and the members failed to establish sufficient injury to confer standing with respect to the other three ordinances, which authorized temporary removal of guns from persons found to pose a risk of imminent harm, which prohibited persons subject to an abuse order from acquiring or possessing guns, and which imposed notice requirements on owners whose guns were lost or stolen. With regards to the remaining two ordinances, while § 6120(a) appeared to have been limited to the lawful use of guns by its terms, the Supreme Court of Pennsylvania had held that the general assembly, through enactment of § 6120(a), had denied all municipalities the power to regulate the ownership, possession, transfer, or transportation of firearms.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Commonwealth v. Richmond Twp.

May 22, 2009, Decided

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Summary judgment granted by Commonwealth v. Richmond Twp., 2010 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 446 (Pa. Commw. Ct., May 28, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Court of ORIGINAL JURISDICTION.
Commonwealth v. Richmond Twp., 917 A.2d 397, 2007 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 67 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant township filed a motion for judgment on the pleadings in a declaratory judgment action against it brought by plaintiff, the Attorney General of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania. The Attorney General asserted that the township violated the Agriculture Code, 3 Pa.C.S. §§ 311-318, by adopting and enforcing an unauthorized local ordinance that prohibited or limited normal agricultural operations (NAOs) without the authority of state law.


OVERVIEW: The suit arose from a complaint made to the Attorney General by certain residents of the township who sought to engage in a chicken operation as a NAO. However, under the township's ordinance, the residents' proposed operation was characterized as an intensive agricultural activity (IAA). In support of its motion, the township argued that it was entitled to a judgment on the pleadings because the Attorney General had failed to aver any facts that would support the conclusion that the township had applied or enforced the ordinance against the residents in a manner inconsistent with state law. The court disagreed, finding that the Attorney General sufficiently averred that the ordinance failed to provide any guidance as to how the township determined when activities associated with a NAO intensified to the level that transformed into an IAA and other ambiguous provisions. The court also found that granting the motion was improper since a factual dispute existed over the term commercial composting, which was not defined in the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court denied the township's motion in its entirety.

 

1792 of 2746 DOCUMENTS



Ake v. Bureau of Prof'l & Occupational Affairs


No. 1103 C.D. 2008


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


974 A.2d 514; 2009 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 229


December 26, 2008, Submitted 
May 20, 2009, Decided 
May 20, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reargument denied by Ake v. Bureau of Prof'l & Occupational Affairs, 2009 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 776 (Pa. Commw. Ct., July 16, 2009)
Appeal denied by Ake v. Bureau of Prof'l & Occupational Affairs, 2009 Pa. LEXIS 2923 (Pa., Dec. 29, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. 1132-55-07. State Agency: Bureau of Professional and Occupational Affairs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner accountant challenged the adjudication of respondent, the Bureau of Professional and Occupational Affairs, State Board of Accountancy (the Board), which revoked the accountant's license and certificate of certified public accountant (CPA) to practice public accounting in Pennsylvania.


OVERVIEW: The Board revoked the accountant's license because of his 2002 criminal harassment conviction in the State of Illinois, which involved him leaving a telephone message indicating his disagreement with homosexuality on the answering machine of an individual who was the executive director of a community organization. On appeal, the accountant asserted that the Board abused its discretion by imposing the maximum penalty of revocation of his CPA credentials and that it erred by finding that he was not rehabilitated from his offending conduct. The court held that the Board had grounds to impose a sanction upon the accountant for violating 63 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 9.9a(a)(5) but that the Board abused its discretion by imposing the most drastic available sanction. The court stated that complete revocation of a CPA's credentials should be a sanction reserved for the worst offenders. The court held that a lesser sanction, such as a short-term suspension of the accountant's license or imposition of a civil penalty was more appropriate, with such sanctions not exceeding the severity of the criminal sanctions imposed for the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the Board's order and remanded the matter to the Board for imposition of a lesser sanction.


 

1793 of 2746 DOCUMENTS



Geryville Materials, Inc. v. Lower Milford Twp. Zoning Hearing Bd.


No. 1823 C.D. 2008


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


972 A.2d 136; 2009 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 221


March 30, 2009, Argued 
May 13, 2009, Decided 
May 13, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Geryville Materials, Inc. v. Lower Milford Twp. Zoning Hearing Bd., 608 Pa. 625, 8 A.3d 347, 2010 Pa. LEXIS 780 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. 2007-C-2540. Common Pleas Court of the County of Lehigh. Varricchio, J.
Geryville Materials, Inc. v. Lower Milford Twp. Zoning Hearing Bd., 2008 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 230 (2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought judicial review in the Lehigh County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania) of the decision of appellee township zoning hearing board (board) denying its challenge to the validity of certain of appellee township's zoning and subdivision ordinances. The trial court affirmed the board's decision, and the landowner sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The landowner said its challenges should be deemed approved because the board did not mail a decision upholding the ordinances within one day, under 53 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 10908(10). The appellate court disagreed because (1) no statutory noncompliance consequence was prescribed, (2) no constitutional violation occurred, (3) the statute was directory, not mandatory, and (4) other measures could cure a violation. If the board's findings were not specific enough, under 53 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 10908(9), the error was harmless because it accepted the landowner's evidence. If certain findings were absent, a remand, not a reversal, was the remedy. Enactment defects did not make the ordinances void ab initio because (1) they were properly recorded, (2) lack of a prior challenge to procedures used to adopt them showed they were obeyed, (3) nearly 3,000 permits issued under them showed they were acquiesced to, (4) ordinances over eight years old existed long enough to presume that notice or acquiescence occurred, and, (5) the turmoil from invalidating ordinances less than eight years old would be more harmful than not applying the void ab initio doctrine.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.


 

1794 of 2746 DOCUMENTS



Quest Land Dev. Group, LLC v. Twp. of Lower Heidelberg


No. 2228 C.D. 2008


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


971 A.2d 540; 2009 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 174


March 30, 2009, Argued 
April 30, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. 08-1018. Common Pleas Court of the County of Berks. Judge Lash, J.
Quest Land Dev. Group, LLC v. Zoning Hearing Bd., 594 Pa. 2, 934 A.2d 686, 2007 Pa. LEXIS 2221 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a developer and a landowner, filed a complaint against appellees, a township and a zoning hearing board, in the Common Pleas Court of the County of Berks (Pennsylvania), alleging that the board's members did not file statements of financial interests as required by 65 Pa.C.S. § 1104. The trial court granted the township's and the board's preliminary objections and dismissed the complaint. The developer and the owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The developer and the owner claimed that as the members of the zoning hearing board failed to file statements of financial interests and failed to take the required oath, as required by § 1104 of the Pennsylvania Public Official and Employee Ethics Act, 65 Pa.C.S. § 1104, they were not vested with the authority of the quasi-judicial office to which they were appointed. Therefore, the board was without authority to render a decision as to the developer's and the owner's request for a special exception, thereby rendering a prior decision which the board issued null and void. As the board's decision was null and void, the developer and the owner alleged that the board failed to timely rule on their special exception application and that the application was, therefore, to be deemed approved. On appeal, the court found that the claims that the board members failed to take an oath or failed to file financial statements did not establish any violation of the developer's and the owner's constitutional rights. Therefore, the void ab initio doctrine was not applicable to the action. Furthermore, the de facto doctrine applied to the action and the board's decision was valid.


OUTCOME: The trial courts' order was affirmed.


 

1795 of 2746 DOCUMENTS



Dep't of Health v. Data-Quest, Inc.


No. 1019 C.D. 2008


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


972 A.2d 74; 2009 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 157


December 10, 2008, Argued 
April 14, 2009, Decided 
April 14, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. 3919. State Agency: Board of Claims.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted petitioner Pennsylvania Department of Health (DOH) permission to file an interlocutory appeal of the order of the Board of Claims (Pennsylvania), which overruled the DOH's preliminary objections to the statement of claim filed by respondent corporation for damages under promissory estoppel and quasi-contract theories for services performed in regard to its development of a software system.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether the Board had subject matter jurisdiction over quasi-contract claims against the Commonwealth that were not based on a written agreement under 62 Pa.C.S. § 1724(a)(1). The DOH argued that 62 Pa.C.S. § 1724(a)(1) plainly granted jurisdiction in the Board only over claims arising from contracts, and that, pursuant to the general definition of "contract" in 62 Pa.C.S. § 103, the Board lacked jurisdiction because no written executed agreement existed between the parties. The corporation argued that the Board's jurisdiction over quasi-contract claims had not been extinguished and that, under the Commonwealth Procurement Code, a contract was not always a written agreement. The court concluded that the Board did not commit an error of law in overruling the DOH's preliminary objections based on lack of subject matter jurisdiction because the court agreed with the corporation that applying the definition of the term "contract" in 62 Pa.C.S. § 103 to the provisions in Chapter 17 would deprive the Board of its ability to determine whether a valid contract existed, either express or implied. Thus, the corporation's quasi-contract claims had to be resolved by the Board.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Board's order and remanded the matter for the Board to proceed with the corporation's claim.


 

1796 of 2746 DOCUMENTS



In re Appeal of Riegelsville


No. 1210 C.D. 2008


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


979 A.2d 399; 2009 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 778


February 24, 2009, Submitted 
March 25, 2009, Decided 
March 25, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Publication Ordered August 4, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. 2007-05905-28-6. Common Pleas Court of the County of Bucks. Goldberg, J.
In re Appeal of Riegelsville, 967 A.2d 1093, 2009 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 138 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant borough appealed an order by the Common Pleas Court of the County of Bucks (Pennsylvania) that affirmed a denial of nunc pro tunc relief by appellee county board of assessment appeals.


OVERVIEW: After the borough acquired three parcels of land from a memorial fund, the board issued a separate assessment notice for each of the parcels that gave new assessment values and listed the reason for each change. The board mistakenly sent the notices to the prior owners, who then forwarded the notices to the borough. Although the borough did not file an appeal, its counsel inquired with the board, prior to the deadline, as to the records relating to the parcels. The board official's response reasonably left the impression that the board was aware of the change in ownership and that it would not be necessary for the borough to follow the formal procedures for correcting disputed information in the notices. When the borough learned that the board had not given the parcels tax exempt status, it sought nunc pro tunc relief. The appellate court found, inter alia, that the statement by the board official created a reasonable presumption that the ownership issue was corrected, and also reasonably implied that the parcels were exempt from taxation under 72 Pa. Stat. Ann. § 5020-204(a)(7). Accordingly, the borough's request to appeal nunc pro tunc should have been granted.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed.


 

1797 of 2746 DOCUMENTS



ARIPPA v. Pa. PUC


No. 1198 C.D. 2007


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


966 A.2d 1204; 2009 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 79


December 10, 2008, Argued 
March 3, 2009, Decided 
March 3, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. P-00052149. State Agency: Public Utility Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a case involving the Alternative Energy Portfolio Standards Act (AEPS), 73 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 1648.1-1648.8, an administrative law judge (ALJ) determined that alternative energy credits produced by non-utility generators (NUGs) were owned by electric distribution companies (EDCs). Respondent Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission (PUC) adopted the ALJ's opinion. Petitioner, a non-profit entity whose members were NUGs, petitioned for review.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the issue was who owned alternative energy credits when a power purchase agreement (PPA) was silent on the issue. The appellate court concluded that the Public Utility Regulatory Policies Act of 1978, Pub. L. No. 95-617, § 2, 92 Stat. 3119 (codified as amended in scattered sections of 15, 16, and 30 U.S.C.S.), which precluded state reformation of PPAs, did not preempt the PUC's authority to determine ownership of alternative energy credits because the PUC had not modified the terms of an existing contract, but had determined ownership of assets which were not previously contemplated. Also, the PUC had jurisdiction because, considering the unique nature of alternative energy credits and the AEPS provision for the PUC's extensive oversight of them, resolving the dispute was not a matter of ordinary contract interpretation, but a process that implicated the PUC's particular expertise. Finally, the PUC did not err in concluding that EDCs owned the credits because the purpose of the AEPS was to encourage the creation and use of energy from alternative sources. Where the EDC had already purchased energy from a NUG, the underlying purpose of the AEPS had been satisfied.


OUTCOME: The PUC's order was affirmed.


 

1798 of 2746 DOCUMENTS



Reese Teleservices, Inc. v. Dep't of Labor & Indus.


No. 2103 C.D. 2007


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


975 A.2d 600; 2009 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 238


January 27, 2009, Argued 
March 3, 2009, Decided 
March 3, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Publication Ordered May 27, 2009.
Reargument denied by Reese Teleservices, Inc. v. Dep't of Labor & Indus., 2009 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 394 (Pa. Commw. Ct., Apr. 28, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. 05-A-0036-1. State Agency: Department of Labor and Industry.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employer petitioned for review of an order of the Pennsylvania Department of Labor and Industry, which denied a review of the employer's compensation contribution rates, and affirmed respondent Pennsylvania Office of Unemployment Compensation Tax Services' transfer of corporation one's experience record and reserve account balance to the employer under the Pennsylvania Unemployment Compensation Law, 43 Pa. Stat. Ann. §§ 751-914.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that the stock in corporation one was purchased by to the employer on December 31, 2002. A 2005 change in ownership of the employer was irrelevant. The finding that the employer was not a new employer was supported by substantial evidence that corporation one's co-owner was a shareholder in the employer. Despite its requests, the employer did not receive corporation one's unemployment compensation claims until the Department found that corporation one's experience record and reserve account balance had to be transferred to the employer. The employer sufficiently raised the issue of the constitutionality of the Department's failure to provide corporation one's notices. The Department did not violate the employer's due process rights. The claim that the employer suffered injury due to the failure to give notice of claims was speculative. Further, the employer failed to raise a constitutionally protected property interest as the delay in transferring the reserve account balance was the direct result of the employer's misrepresentations to the Department that there was no common ownership between the employer and corporation one at the time of its transfer.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.


 

1799 of 2746 DOCUMENTS


Zerby v. Shanon


No. 1179 C.D. 2008


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


964 A.2d 956; 2009 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 22


December 12, 2008, Submitted 
February 3, 2009, Decided 
February 3, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. Parole No. 849-DM. State Agency: Board of Probation and Parole.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate challenged the decision of respondent Pennsylvania Board of Probation and Parole to recalculate his maximum incarceration date. The inmate's counsel filed an application for leave to withdraw from representation of the inmate the ground that the inmate's petition for review was frivolous.


OVERVIEW: Counsel seeking to withdraw from representation of a petitioner seeking review of the Board's determination had to provide a "no-merit" letter, detailing the nature and extent of counsel's review and listing each issue the inmate wished to raise, with counsel's explanation of why those issues were meritless. The commonwealth court held that counsel's no-merit letter did not address all of the inmate's arguments and did not provide a substantive explanation of why the issues it did raise were meritless. Although the inmate's claim that he was not advised that the Board would be able to alter his plea agreement could be meritless, it was still incumbent upon counsel to include it in the no-merit letter and explain why it was meritless. While the letter did cite statutory authority for the principle that the inmate could not serve his State and county sentences at the same time, it did not provide any substantive authority supporting the Board's determination that the inmate was not available to serve his State sentence until April 22, 2008, even though the Board had already recommitted him as of July 25, 2007.


OUTCOME: The commonwealth court denied counsel's application for leave to withdraw without prejudice and granted counsel thirty days from the date of the order to either file a renewed application to withdraw, along with an amended no-merit letter, or submit a brief on the merits of the inmate's petition for review.

 

1800 of 2746 DOCUMENTS



Commonwealth v. Gavlock


No. 873 C.D. 2008


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


964 A.2d 455; 2008 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 629


December 8, 2008, Argued 
December 31, 2008, Decided 
December 31, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Amended by Commonwealth v. Gavlock, 2009 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 2 (Pa. Commw. Ct., Jan. 5, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from No. SA 20-2007. Common Pleas Court of the County of Clinton. Williamson, President Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner appealed an order by the Common Pleas Court of the County of Clinton (Pennsylvania) that fined him $ 500 for violating 34 Pa. C.S. §2307(a); the owner claimed, inter alia, that 34 Pa. C.S. §§2307 and 2121 impermissibly infringed upon his constitutional rights to protect his property against damage and to equal protection under the law, and that the verdict was against the weight of the evidence presented at trial.


OVERVIEW: The owner shot and killed an elk that was allegedly eating one of his fruit trees during the closed season. Thereafter, the owner was cited the owner for killing an elk out of season. The owner testified that he would not use the non-lethal ways to discourage elk from entering his property because he was told that the Commission was out of money and that the cracker shot and rubber pellets could damage his gun. The owner acknowledged that he did not cultivate his fruit trees as a primary means of gaining his livelihood, and, thus, he was not a "person" entitled to the exception to §2307 set forth in §2121(a). Although the owner observed the same elk on his property for a week, and, although he was concerned that the elk would damage his fruit trees, he did not contact the Commission or take any other protective measures before shooting the elk. The appellate court found that, under the circumstances, the trial court properly fined the owner for shooting the elk during the closed season without justification. The appellate court declined to address either of the constitutional issues or the owner's evidentiary issue.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.
